<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer3281716776824063019">#1 New York Times bestselling author, Nelson DeMille, delivers an explosive thriller of international intrigue and high-voltage political tension set in contemporary Russia.On a dark road deep inside Russia, a young American tourist picks up a most unusual passenger a U.S. POW on the run with an incredible secret to reveal to an unsuspecting world. The secret concerns "The</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3281716776824063019">#1 New York Times bestselling author, Nelson DeMille, delivers an explosive thriller of international intrigue and high-voltage political tension set in contemporary Russia.On a dark road deep inside Russia, a young American tourist picks up a most unusual passenger a U.S. POW on the run with an incredible secret to reveal to an unsuspecting world. The secret concerns "The Charm School," a vast and astounding KGB conspiracy that stands poised against the very heartland of America. Arrayed against this renegade power of the Soviet state are three Americans: an Air Force officer, who will fly one last covert mission into the center of a mad experiment; an embassy liaison, who will have her hopes for a saner superpower balance brutally tested; and the chief of the CIA's Moscow station, who will find his intricate dance of destiny and death reaching its devastating conclusion.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3281716776824063019">...more</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7668522-carol" class="user" title="Carol">Carol</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer345514301">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4922486729147956761">When a young American tourist <em>(Gregory Fisher)</em> picks up a U.S. POW on the run while touring Russia, <em>(in his Pontiac Grand Am)</em> the excitement begins and doesn't stop.<p>This intense and fast-moving spy thriller brings the evil of the Soviet Union to life during the Cold War with well-defined characters, loads of KGB treachery and a horror of a secret deep in the woods.</p><p>Perhaps a little wordy at times, and I did not care much for the female protagonist, but the brave Colonel Hollis and his sarcastic w</p></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4922486729147956761">When a young American tourist <em>(Gregory Fisher)</em> picks up a U.S. POW on the run while touring Russia, <em>(in his Pontiac Grand Am)</em> the excitement begins and doesn't stop.<p>This intense and fast-moving spy thriller brings the evil of the Soviet Union to life during the Cold War with well-defined characters, loads of KGB treachery and a horror of a secret deep in the woods.</p><p>Perhaps a little wordy at times, and I did not care much for the female protagonist, but the brave Colonel Hollis and his sarcastic wit more than made up for her weaknesses in spades. Unputdownable.....despite the near 800 pages and one of my favorites by DeMille. 4.5 Stars.</p><p>
  <strong>Update: March 24, 2015</strong>
</p><p>Oops! Forgot to mention.......Erik Larson even makes an appearance!</p></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1083932899">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1083932899" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5117003-checkman" class="left imgcol" title="Checkman"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442122856p2/5117003.jpg" alt="Checkman" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1083932899?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 28, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5117003-checkman" class="user" title="Checkman">Checkman</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/353814.The_Charm_School" title="Paperback 9780751531183" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5117003-checkman?shelf=espionage" class="actionLinkLite">espionage</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5117003-checkman?shelf=action" class="actionLinkLite">action</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5117003-checkman?shelf=beach-read" class="actionLinkLite">beach-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1083932899">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4233413760103951940">Approximately twenty to twenty-five years (lets say from about 1986-1994) ago I was a big fan of Nelson DeMille.I would purchase his newest novels when they appeared on the shelves and I searched for his older novels (pre-1986) in my favorite used bookstores. Eventually I changed and DeMille's books changed and I drifted away,but the fond memories remained.<br /><br /><em> The Charm School</em> was one of my favorites.I read it in 1989 when I was twenty-one. I remember it being an intelligent and observant novel wit</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4233413760103951940">Approximately twenty to twenty-five years (lets say from about 1986-1994) ago I was a big fan of Nelson DeMille.I would purchase his newest novels when they appeared on the shelves and I searched for his older novels (pre-1986) in my favorite used bookstores. Eventually I changed and DeMille's books changed and I drifted away,but the fond memories remained.<br /><br /><em> The Charm School</em> was one of my favorites.I read it in 1989 when I was twenty-one. I remember it being an intelligent and observant novel with something to say about politics, humanity and war. It seemed very deep and it wrapped up with a very satisfying slam-bang conclusion. <br /><br />A couple months ago I returned to this book. Now remember I last read it in 1989. I knew that it would be dated. The world's political setting has seen dramatic changes in the past twenty-five years as has my personal life. My wife and I are still together, but much has changed to include my economic status (it has gotten better thankfully), my career path (I was Army in 89), and my ideals (more moderate and realistic). Keeping these things in mind I returned to my younger days. This is always a risky proposal. <a title="Thomas Wolfe" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7921.Thomas_Wolfe">Thomas Wolfe</a> understood that, but I went ahead anyway.<br /><br />What did I find? Well it's still an entertaining Cold War espionage thriller in terms of the plot. Implausible, but then how many "edge of your seat" espionage thrillers are plausible? As mentioned earlier it was dated, but that wasn't an issue for me. What I didn't like was the hero. He was a sarcastic jerk who was unlikable and something of an idiot who caused as many problems as he solved and would have been ejected by the Soviet Union as being unwelcomed. I got through the book, but when the hero is unlikabe it makes it difficult to keep with a story which is why it took me two months to finish it.<br /><br />Over the last couple days I've scanned the few DeMille books that I have held onto and I now understand why I stopped reading him. All his heroes are insufferable sarcastic a-holes. They read like smartmouth seventeen year old boys and I don't like sarcastic seventeen year old boys (or girls). <br /><br />At the time I might not have been aware of what was going on, but I was growing up during the years that I read DeMille. As a young man I believed that sarcasm passed for intelligence and wit, but I grew up. I came to the realization that in the adult world uncontrolled sarcasm and a smartass attitude will hurt you and impede you. In other words I changed, but DeMille's heroes didn't.All of his heroes are basically the same person with just a different plot and name. <br /><br />Well another cherished memory from my younger days shot down in flames. I've got to stop doing that. *sigh*<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4233413760103951940">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/2806902-chipper" class="user" title="Chipper">Chipper</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer253858918">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16732298231009089041">A spy-mystery from Demille, when Demille was a younger writer still developing his sarcastic wit. Even then, he could make a seemingly improbable story believable and highly entertaining. For anyone over 40 who remembers the tail-end of the long and mistrust-filled Cold War, this book will resonate.<br /><br />As usual, DeMille weaves an imaginative story involving characters you love, spies in the late 1980's, the American Embassy in Moscow, a bit of Russian history, Vietnam MIAs, a training school for Sov</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16732298231009089041">A spy-mystery from Demille, when Demille was a younger writer still developing his sarcastic wit. Even then, he could make a seemingly improbable story believable and highly entertaining. For anyone over 40 who remembers the tail-end of the long and mistrust-filled Cold War, this book will resonate.<br /><br />As usual, DeMille weaves an imaginative story involving characters you love, spies in the late 1980's, the American Embassy in Moscow, a bit of Russian history, Vietnam MIAs, a training school for Soviet Spies and a rescue mission that will have you on the edge of your seat. The Charm School is riveting and one his best finishes, reminiscent of Night Fall and Plum Island. Could the Charm School have ever existed?</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16732298231009089041">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer8100673199499818899">This is one doozy of a spy novel! Especially for those of us who grew up during the Cold War and remember how mistrustful we were of the Russkies. <br /><br />I read this in print many years ago and just recently listened to the audio version. I've read several of this author's novels in the John Corey series, but this stand alone trumps them all. I believe it was his first novel (??), and I think it's his best. <br /><br />Sam Hollis and Lisa Rhodes work at the American embassy in Moscow. They stumble upon information</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8100673199499818899">This is one doozy of a spy novel! Especially for those of us who grew up during the Cold War and remember how mistrustful we were of the Russkies. <br /><br />I read this in print many years ago and just recently listened to the audio version. I've read several of this author's novels in the John Corey series, but this stand alone trumps them all. I believe it was his first novel (??), and I think it's his best. <br /><br />Sam Hollis and Lisa Rhodes work at the American embassy in Moscow. They stumble upon information about a secret "school" in Russia where Americans are held against their will and have to teach Russians how to pass as Americans. They study language and slang and history and culture, and then are sent to the U.S. where they live as Americans and are gradually infiltrating all levels of society.<br /><br />As always, DeMille can be a little long winded, but he clearly did his research about Russia. Much of it is quite interesting, and rather prescient considering this was published before the Berlin Wall came down. I found the ending more satisfying than some of DeMille's other novels.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/706652965?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 29, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/23503840-cautious-reader" class="user" title="Cautious Reader">Cautious Reader</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/353814.The_Charm_School" title="Paperback 9780751531183" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer706652965">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13502741678112234553">This book is one of those that you wish could be made into a good movie. Oh wait a second… have you see a new TV series The Americans? I bet the idea for The Americans came from The Charm School. You know… the idea of Russian spies infiltrating the US, pretending to be Americans? Scared already? By the way, The Americans is one clever TV show that is such a rarity in our modern TV world.<br /><br />If you like spy novels, you might love The Charm School. I am not a big fan of anything spies related. Unless</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13502741678112234553">This book is one of those that you wish could be made into a good movie. Oh wait a second… have you see a new TV series The Americans? I bet the idea for The Americans came from The Charm School. You know… the idea of Russian spies infiltrating the US, pretending to be Americans? Scared already? By the way, The Americans is one clever TV show that is such a rarity in our modern TV world.<br /><br />If you like spy novels, you might love The Charm School. I am not a big fan of anything spies related. Unless it is Daniel Craig as James Bond. Unless it is a clever TV show. Unless it is a well-written book.<br /><br />The Charm School is just that – a very well written spy novel. We have a hero. We have a cold blooded son-of-a-bitch anti-hero. We have brutal Russian KGB agents. We have a smart ass American spy. We have a psychotic Russian spy. We have a love triangle. We have car chases, torture chambers, spy equipment, and Russian essential elements such as vodka and borsch. We have it all in this book.<br /><br />It was not a wild ride as you might think, but it was an intense one. The ending was not as impressive as the book itself. It seemed rushed. It seemed that DeMille got tired with his own story and decided to wrap it up on a whim. It did take a little bit away from the book but not much.<br /><br />One final thought – curiosity is a root of all espionage. If you are curious, go ahead and read The Charm School. You won’t regret it.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13502741678112234553">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_662177222">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/662177222" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1721356-ioana" class="left imgcol" title="Ioana"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451618243p2/1721356.jpg" alt="Ioana" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/662177222?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 02, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1721356-ioana" class="user" title="Ioana">Ioana</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/353814.The_Charm_School" title="Paperback 9780751531183" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1721356-ioana?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1721356-ioana?shelf=pulp" class="actionLinkLite">pulp</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1721356-ioana?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1721356-ioana?shelf=communism" class="actionLinkLite">communism</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1721356-ioana?shelf=espionage" class="actionLinkLite">espionage</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer662177222">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10913739055921720939">2.5 but deserves to be rounded down to 2 rather than up to 3; my first DeMille book and convinced me to NEVER read him again.<br /><br />This is a harsh rating for a relatively well written book; for pulp, the use of language and research doesn't get much better than this. However, the author (and his self importance and conceit), the characters, the characterization of the USSR, the work's long winded-ness, and its portrayal of relationships annoyed me so much as to push my rating over the edge.<br /><br />#1: It real</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10913739055921720939">2.5 but deserves to be rounded down to 2 rather than up to 3; my first DeMille book and convinced me to NEVER read him again.<br /><br />This is a harsh rating for a relatively well written book; for pulp, the use of language and research doesn't get much better than this. However, the author (and his self importance and conceit), the characters, the characterization of the USSR, the work's long winded-ness, and its portrayal of relationships annoyed me so much as to push my rating over the edge.<br /><br />#1: It really took a lot of effort for me to give this book a shot after reading the second paragraph of the author's intro: "The Cold War is over, so is The Charm School still relevant? ... The Iliad is still read almost 3000 years after it first appeared...." UM Get a grip Mr. DeMille, you are no Homer, and even if you were, it would not be for you to characterize yourself as such. <br /><br />#2: The characters are TRULY detestable, each and every single one of them; although clearly DeMille is trying to portray Americans as somehow superior to the Russians, everyone from Hollis to Lisa to Alevy to every American in between comes off as naive, idiotic, self aggrandizing, or worse. <br />Example #1: in the middle of a time sensitive critical operation in which Alevy is saving Lisa and Hollis from a KGB camp, Lisa stops to ask Alevy in a whiny typically sexist portrayal, "do you know what [the Russians] did to me" in this camp? Well, honey, I bet he does have some ideas, and even if he does not, is this really the time to begin this (or ANY) discussion? <br />Example #2: Hollis first wants to rescue some American POWs gone missing for decades, then when he meets them in person he is contemptible, cruel, and cold towards them for being "traitors" while doing exactly what the POWs are doing (ie being a "traitor" himself), and finally he returns to detesting his government and wanting to hold them accountable for not dealing with these "traitors" in a way he condones... <br /><br />#3: The characterization of the USSR really got to me; I grew up in communist Romania, and my family suffered a great deal as a consequence (we are political refugees in the USA, long story). There's a lot of similarities between the Romanian and USSR regimes, and DeMille does a good job portraying all Russians as either cruel animals, pathetic impotents, sellouts, or any other number of unflattering characterizations. There is not ONE positive portrayal of a Russian: if there are any in the book who are not evil by DeMille's standards, then they are just pathetic excuses for human beings who are too stupid/naive/unable to help themselves (even Zurikov, the defector, is portrayed as such even though Hollis comes to the conclusion at some point that he "just wants to be free, whatever that freedom means to him"...)... A lot of people in the USSR/eastern block suffered a GREAT DEAL at communist hands (I would argue, a majority), and yes, there was very little that could be done unfortunately until conditions changed in the late 80s; people resisted in their own ways: poetry, humor, underground art and radio, black market economies. Just because they were not able to take concrete action by democratic standards and overthrow totalitarianism sooner does not make all eastern europeans naive, impotent, cruel, or idiotic...<br /><br />#4: The book just goes on and on and on and on... even though very little actually happens. I guess part of it is to build atmosphere but it's TOO much! <br /><br />#5: The relationships are totally, entirely unbelievable, starting with the romance between Lisa and Hollis (20 years apart), which is completely unexplainable and unrealistic... I NEVER got why they "loved" each other, the attraction was incredibly superficial, etc. Same with most other relationships in the book.<br /><br />That said, it WAS a good mystery that was written fairly well: IF it had been condensed into about half the space and IF it had left out some of the snark, bad attempt at creating relationships, and anti-people-who-are-oppressed propaganda, I probably would have rated this a 4. As it stood, however, it's a 2, and it also has helped me form my opinion of DeMille as an author I will NOT try again. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10913739055921720939">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_133125364">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/133125364" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4262996-kate-woods-walker" class="left imgcol" title="Kate Woods Walker"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1283964615p2/4262996.jpg" alt="Kate Woods Walker" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/133125364?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 28, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4262996-kate-woods-walker" class="user" title="Kate Woods Walker">Kate Woods Walker</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/353814.The_Charm_School" title="Paperback 9780751531183" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer133125364">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2304729711717486683">Turgid exposition that describes every plodding step our hero makes, hamhanded propaganda, one cardboard woman who would be right at home on Mickey Spillaine's lap, Soviet villains who display every Reagan-era leitmotif Americans were conditioned to despise (until we turned the tables in the Bush era and <em>became </em> the torturing, anti-due process monsters we once fought)--what's not to loathe about this book? <br /><br />Author Nelson DeMille <em>did</em> manage to create a bit of mounting suspense, with some nifty wri</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2304729711717486683">Turgid exposition that describes every plodding step our hero makes, hamhanded propaganda, one cardboard woman who would be right at home on Mickey Spillaine's lap, Soviet villains who display every Reagan-era leitmotif Americans were conditioned to despise (until we turned the tables in the Bush era and <em>became </em> the torturing, anti-due process monsters we once fought)--what's not to loathe about this book? <br /><br />Author Nelson DeMille <em>did</em> manage to create a bit of mounting suspense, with some nifty writing in alternating settings at the beginning of Part V, the most action-packed section of this hairy-chested man's book. But he lost all he gained once the action started. DeMille felt the need to describe--in great detail--each nook and cranny of the weaponry.<br /><br />The plot itself is standard-issue action adventure, with an anti-diplomacy twist at the end that leaves any conscience-burdened reader saying "WTF?". And if all the steel-jawed murder is not enough to repel readers, there's some pretty blatant anti-Semitism too.<br /><br />I can't think of any circumstance, short of Soviet-era or Bush-era torture, that would cause me to recommend this book.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2304729711717486683">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_341570057">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/341570057" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6969151-veeral" class="left imgcol" title="Veeral"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1344326461p2/6969151.jpg" alt="Veeral" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/341570057?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 20, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6969151-veeral" class="user" title="Veeral">Veeral</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/353814.The_Charm_School" title="Paperback 9780751531183" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6969151-veeral?shelf=spy-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">spy-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6969151-veeral?shelf=thriller" class="actionLinkLite">thriller</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6969151-veeral?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6969151-veeral?shelf=read-in-2013" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6969151-veeral?shelf=woolly-mammoths" class="actionLinkLite">woolly-mammoths</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6969151-veeral?shelf=800-1000-pages" class="actionLinkLite">800-1000-pages</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer341570057">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15578543737770647475">Welcome to Mrs. Ivanova's Charm School, a top secret "facility" where they teach Russian spies to pass themselves off as Americans to even a real American. Then off to the US of A with a fake identity (Non-Russian, of course) where they would live as American citizens and would pass on the state secrets to their homeland and gradually, would get a virtual hold on the entire country. Who would teach them? The MIAs (missing in action) from the Vietnam War who were captured and flown illegitimately</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15578543737770647475">Welcome to Mrs. Ivanova's Charm School, a top secret "facility" where they teach Russian spies to pass themselves off as Americans to even a real American. Then off to the US of A with a fake identity (Non-Russian, of course) where they would live as American citizens and would pass on the state secrets to their homeland and gradually, would get a virtual hold on the entire country. Who would teach them? The MIAs (missing in action) from the Vietnam War who were captured and flown illegitimately to the USSR from Vietnam.<br /><br />*********************************************************<br /><br />I read this book purely because of the subject matter it dealt with. Have you ever wondered what happens to a soldier when he is considered MIA in any war? If luck is on his side, then he is probably dead. But if it is not, it's more than likely that the enemy has him and they are not going to acknowledge his existence. Ever. And sadly, there is little one can do about that as there is bound to be a severe lack of evidence to raise any legitimate inquiry. <br /><br />But more often than not, it's incompetency and cavalier attitude on the part of that country's politicians that these men are doomed to live as prisoners for life. After all, they have served their purpose of fighting a war for their country, but now it's time for the peace talks and improving relations, so such minor and inconsequential hurdles should be ignored for the "greater" good. <br /><br />Look on the web and you will not find a single country which has fought a war that is not being accused of wrongfully imprisoning MIAs of its enemies and denying their existence. Think of the devastation it may wrought on the psyche of the family members of that MIA who are never going to know for sure whether their beloved one is dead or alive.<br /><br />So regardless of your nationality, try to spare a moment and think about these poor souls, because if your country has fought a war in the past 35-50 years, chances are that some of your countrymen who were listed as MIA at that time are still alive and being tortured daily for their patriotism.<br /><br />*********************************************************<br /><br />Now about <a title="The Charm School by Nelson DeMille" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/353814.The_Charm_School">The Charm School</a>. "The Charm School" felt 200 pages too long. Normal dialogues between characters seemed rather clunky to me. Especially intimate conversation between the main characters Sam Hollis and Lisa Rhodes felt really gawky most of the times. But I liked the dry witticism that <a title="Nelson DeMille" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1238.Nelson_DeMille">Nelson DeMille</a> has apparently deemed essential to render to almost all of his characters whenever they were trying to outfox each other. Sadly, all the Russians were depicted stereo-typically in the book. I would have liked to see better developed characters on the Russian side. <br /><br />But thankfully, last 100 pages were very exciting and the ending also seemed quiet logical to me.<br /><br /><strong>4 stars</strong></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15578543737770647475">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer496745777">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5206832644489391001">I don't think I've given one star before but this book was such a disappointment I can't possibly do anything else. I've read and enjoyed a couple of other thrillers by this author, so I gave him the benefit of the doubt and persisted with this stinker -- but my perseverance was not rewarded. I realize it was written in the late 1980s, but even so the evil Russians and the noble Americans (complete with flaws of course, since shucks, nobody's perfect)were caricatures from a comic book in the 195</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5206832644489391001">I don't think I've given one star before but this book was such a disappointment I can't possibly do anything else. I've read and enjoyed a couple of other thrillers by this author, so I gave him the benefit of the doubt and persisted with this stinker -- but my perseverance was not rewarded. I realize it was written in the late 1980s, but even so the evil Russians and the noble Americans (complete with flaws of course, since shucks, nobody's perfect)were caricatures from a comic book in the 1950s. I didn't like the Russians, I didn't like the Americans, and the whole Cold-War breathless "aren't they horrible?" stuff that went on and on was ludicrous. And this criticism isn't just because the world has moved on and we have other super villains. I've read and been enthralled by LeCarre, for instance, since the fall of the Berlin Wall. This book is two-dimensional and I'm really sorry I wasted my time.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_228772436">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/228772436" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2747498-arun-divakar" class="left imgcol" title="Arun Divakar"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1253201408p2/2747498.jpg" alt="Arun Divakar" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/228772436?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 06, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2747498-arun-divakar" class="user" title="Arun Divakar">Arun Divakar</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/353814.The_Charm_School" title="Paperback 9780751531183" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer228772436">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11629752972920652257">Espionage stories set during the premise of the cold war are probably the most alluring of all backdrops that thriller writers can think of. Two of the world's super powers while in all external appearances behaved like bosom buddies hid daggers beneath their smiles and behind closed rooms plotted how to outwit each other. While this was going on the world would have lived in perennial trepidation of an impending holocaust. But then in 1991, the USSR vanished and the soviet bloc suddenly ceased</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11629752972920652257">Espionage stories set during the premise of the cold war are probably the most alluring of all backdrops that thriller writers can think of. Two of the world's super powers while in all external appearances behaved like bosom buddies hid daggers beneath their smiles and behind closed rooms plotted how to outwit each other. While this was going on the world would have lived in perennial trepidation of an impending holocaust. But then in 1991, the USSR vanished and the soviet bloc suddenly ceased to exist. As easy as it sounds, the threat disappeared &amp; the Americans moved on to get involved in other bigger messes. Interesting isn't it ? Many authors seem to think so too judging by the number of spy thrillers out there &amp; I admit to the fact that I am a sucker for them !<br /><br />Simply put, the plot line is : <em>Invasion of the body snatchers meets cloak &amp; dagger espionage </em>. The KGB on the path to world domination through a massive intelligence offensive and the Americans out to stop them is what it is all about. The first 100 pages showed a lot of promise in this plot and then as suddenly as it had appeared, the promise disappeared. DeMille puts a lot of focus on Russia during the Cold War era and to his credit I must say that the plot covers some of the pros and the cons of this enigmatic landscape. The characters are thoroughly one dimensional and forgettable with the good being startlingly brilliant shades of white and evil being hey-who-turned-out-the-lights black. For a novel which some one termed as a gem in cold war literature, this had some of the mushiest romantic scenes I have ever read. Bleh !<br /><br />The best parts are the dialog between the characters for Demille writes some of the wittiest verbal banter which alternates between the cheeky to the chuckle out loud kind of humor. I would recommend this as an entertainer,akin to the kind of movies Roland Emmerich makes (minus the explosions that is !).</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11629752972920652257">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_590477227">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/590477227" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7573688-r-l-anderson" class="left imgcol" title="R.L. Anderson"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1335389850p2/7573688.jpg" alt="R.L. Anderson" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/590477227?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 14, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7573688-r-l-anderson" class="user" title="R.L. Anderson">R.L. Anderson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/353814.The_Charm_School" title="Paperback 9780751531183" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer590477227">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6805096886769416502">One of the best Cold War thrillers ever! A real page turner that I couldn't put down. Also very educational, as it describes details of the lives of American diplomats working in a US embassy in a hostile (at the time) nation, the old Soviet Union. One little detail that sticks in my mind is the mention that US diplomats are some of the most patriotic Americans you could ever hope to meet--but yet they are just not "into" the popular culture. Hmmmmm.... That sounds strange, doesn't it? Well--the</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6805096886769416502">One of the best Cold War thrillers ever! A real page turner that I couldn't put down. Also very educational, as it describes details of the lives of American diplomats working in a US embassy in a hostile (at the time) nation, the old Soviet Union. One little detail that sticks in my mind is the mention that US diplomats are some of the most patriotic Americans you could ever hope to meet--but yet they are just not "into" the popular culture. Hmmmmm.... That sounds strange, doesn't it? Well--the more thought I gave to it, the more I realized that I am very much that way myself!!! Guess I'd make a good member of the Diplomatic Corps. This is an excellent book and one of many I've read that gradually steered me away from sci fi, which I had been a big fan of as a kid, and into the mystery genre. I am now writing mysteries, myself, Ranch Park, It's A Place For Trees, and Viking It Is--although mine are of a much more tame domestic nature, as I don't have the knowledge and experience in international affairs to be able to write an international thriller such as this. Nelson DeMille shows that he is truly an expert in this field. Maybe I will be someday when I have the opportunity to do more traveling. The Charm School comes highly recommended by this mystery author of a very different kind of mystery. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6805096886769416502">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3878584641057648720">L'ho letto in italiano anche se l'edizione italiana non esiste, non c'è nei book store. Misteri della rete.<br />E' un spy story del 1988, quindi scritto prima della caduta del muro. E infatti c'è tutta l'URSS del KGB, così come l'immaginava l'occidente.<br />Il mistero della scomparsa di un ragazzo americano scatena la ricerca di un'oasi "statunitense" vicino a Mosca, ma tutto si svolge con estrema discrezione per non compromettere i colloqui distensivi tra le due superpotenze.<br /><br />Questo libro sembra archeolog</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3878584641057648720">L'ho letto in italiano anche se l'edizione italiana non esiste, non c'è nei book store. Misteri della rete.<br />E' un spy story del 1988, quindi scritto prima della caduta del muro. E infatti c'è tutta l'URSS del KGB, così come l'immaginava l'occidente.<br />Il mistero della scomparsa di un ragazzo americano scatena la ricerca di un'oasi "statunitense" vicino a Mosca, ma tutto si svolge con estrema discrezione per non compromettere i colloqui distensivi tra le due superpotenze.<br /><br />Questo libro sembra archeologia perché oggi, con tutta probabilità, gli interessi spionistici sono orientati altrove, ma basti pensare alla deposizione di Nicu Ceau?escu, e quello che è stato trovato nelle sale di tortura rumene, per rendersi conto che la fiction non si discosta poi molto dalla realtà.<br /><br />Si legge d'un fiato, scritto bene. L'edizione che ho letto è circa la metà delle pagine dell'originale.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_230796388">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/230796388" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4792672-brian" class="left imgcol" title="Brian"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1321711943p2/4792672.jpg" alt="Brian" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/230796388?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 03, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4792672-brian" class="user" title="Brian">Brian</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/353814.The_Charm_School" title="Paperback 9780751531183" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer230796388">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3162062824386763812">* One of the last Cold War novels of the Cold War period. Published in 1988, the book, with its POW/MIA theme--and its setting in a mighty USSR--is situated more comfortably in the decade of Rambo than in the political reality of the late eighties/early nineties. In '89, the Berlin Wall came down and in '91, the Soviet Union was officially dissolved. In this context, it's amusing, in a way, and quite impossible to take seriously. Fortunately, this is fiction and none of that really matters. Exce</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3162062824386763812">* One of the last Cold War novels of the Cold War period. Published in 1988, the book, with its POW/MIA theme--and its setting in a mighty USSR--is situated more comfortably in the decade of Rambo than in the political reality of the late eighties/early nineties. In '89, the Berlin Wall came down and in '91, the Soviet Union was officially dissolved. In this context, it's amusing, in a way, and quite impossible to take seriously. Fortunately, this is fiction and none of that really matters. Except for some of the technology, this could just as easily have been written two or three decades earlier. Spiritually, it stands alongside The Manchurian Candidate, and evokes memories of an earlier time and a different, in some ways more frightening, world.<br /><br />* Sure, it's too long, but that's less a criticism than an observation of style. The hero, Sam Hollis, may be a man of few words, but pithiness isn't really part of DeMille's literary toolbox. For one thing, I enjoyed many of the book's lengthy dialogues, which reminded me of all the times, in other books, I've wondered just when it was that the characters actually communicated to each other something besides plot points.<br /><br />* Speaking of plot, though...What had to happen was simple: the Charm School itself had to live up to the opening of the novel, which is when we first hear of it. The opening is a wonderful grabber, both spooky and full of impending doom. But a lot of books start out well--because there's still a sense of mystery. The real test is what happens when the veils start to fall. Here, DeMille seems to have started with the Charm School, his central mystery, and then worked backward to that terrific opening. True, when all is revealed, it's no longer spooky, exactly, but it's just as dreadful.<br /><br />* Don't expect complex characters or deep political philosophy, of course: this is a thriller, after all. But there's enough ambiguity so that if you take the time to think about it (not required), you can come up with some pretty interesting questions.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3162062824386763812">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_180559874">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/180559874" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3095102-gerald-sinstadt" class="left imgcol" title="Gerald Sinstadt"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1272455057p2/3095102.jpg" alt="Gerald Sinstadt" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/180559874?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 13, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3095102-gerald-sinstadt" class="user" title="Gerald Sinstadt">Gerald Sinstadt</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/353814.The_Charm_School" title="Paperback 9780751531183" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3095102-gerald-sinstadt?shelf=crime" class="actionLinkLite">crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer180559874">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12455938506600019837">Nelson DeMille, a versatile author whose Long Island adventure yarns make good reading, is proud of The Charm School, pointing out in an introduction that it has been in print since 1988. The setting is the Soviet Union of that era. Colonel Sam Hollis, an attaché at the US Embassy in Moscow, is in fact a spy. Ill-advisedly - not to say improbably - his attraction for Lisa Rhodes, a member of the Information Staff, leads him to allow her to become his espionage side-kick. They investigate a myste</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12455938506600019837">Nelson DeMille, a versatile author whose Long Island adventure yarns make good reading, is proud of The Charm School, pointing out in an introduction that it has been in print since 1988. The setting is the Soviet Union of that era. Colonel Sam Hollis, an attaché at the US Embassy in Moscow, is in fact a spy. Ill-advisedly - not to say improbably - his attraction for Lisa Rhodes, a member of the Information Staff, leads him to allow her to become his espionage side-kick. They investigate a mysterious, off-limits Soviet encampment near Borodino. When they are discovered, Hollis kills two KGB guards. From there, the plot curdles until Sam and Lisa find themselves prisoners on the inside of what is the Charm School of the book's title. <br /><br />There are many twists, betrayal and duplicity, violence and killing. By the end, the murder count is beyond reckoning, beyond believing. Yet the pace only quickens in bursts. This is a book of 700 pages. There are times when it reads like a guide to life in the Soviet Union in the 1980s. Religion and iconography are explored. In later chapters technical details confronting a pilot in flight are lengthy and best skimmed through. Above all, no opportunity is lost to draw comparisons between Soviet tyranny and the Way of Life in the Land of the Free. Guess which of the two regimes the reader is invited to admire? <br /><br />A reluctant third star was almost withheld because of a writer's tic that grew more irritating with each repetition. DeMille frequently dilutes a noun with 'rather.' Something is "rather embarrassing," someone is "rather good-looking," (or else "rather short'), an atmosphere is "rather nice," a party is "rather uninhibited." Simply strike out 'rather' in those and all the other examples and see if the meaning is damaged. The same could be said of "somewhat forlorn," "somewhat calmer," "Somewhat better," "somewhat important," "somewhat surprised," etc, etc. <br /><br />Maybe DeMille wrote before Universities ran Creative Writing courses.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12455938506600019837">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/468286960" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/343908-elizabeth" class="left imgcol" title="Elizabeth"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1189716402p2/343908.jpg" alt="Elizabeth" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/468286960?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 02, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/343908-elizabeth" class="user" title="Elizabeth">Elizabeth</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/353814.The_Charm_School" title="Paperback 9780751531183" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer468286960">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1127658977428782927">The unlikely premise of this thriller is so scary and diabolical that it draws you into the book like a magnet. What if there was a school in Russia that trained Russians how to be Americans? What if those "Americans" were mainstreamed into our society to "report back" to Russia? What if the instructors @ this supposed "Charm School" were POWs from the Vietnam War? This is a 536 page book that I could not put down. I loved the fact that the characters' behaviors were impossible to predict. Also,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1127658977428782927">The unlikely premise of this thriller is so scary and diabolical that it draws you into the book like a magnet. What if there was a school in Russia that trained Russians how to be Americans? What if those "Americans" were mainstreamed into our society to "report back" to Russia? What if the instructors @ this supposed "Charm School" were POWs from the Vietnam War? This is a 536 page book that I could not put down. I loved the fact that the characters' behaviors were impossible to predict. Also, the politics in both Russia and the United States was intricately complicated and held consequences for both the operatives and innocent victims. I really liked that nothing was ever as it seemed. This was a great exercise for the brain in addition to be entertaining. I can't wait to try another by this author. Thanks to Rick Cohler for the rec! I would enjoy this book being made into a film. There was a film running inside my head the entire time I was reading it.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1127658977428782927">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5187313220261441881">As excitimg as a Friday night trip to the landromat and watching your clothes dry. Rarely do I not finish a book. This has consistently good reviews, but I just couldn't get into it. I quit at 30%--275 pages. Even at that point he still hadn't gotten into the plot and was still introducing major characters.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText5187313220261441881">As excitimg as a Friday night trip to the landromat and watching your clothes dry. Rarely do I not finish a book. This has consistently good reviews, but I just couldn't get into it. I quit at 30%--275 pages. Even at that point he still hadn't gotten into the plot and was still introducing major characters. Readers have said that this is a page-turner from beginning to end. I just didn't see the page-turner part, unless you were turning them just to skip.<br /><br />The premice seemed interesting enough...if it had only just got going. Most of what I read was simply a diatribe on Soviet totalitarianism, brutality, suspicion and repression. I've read that history already. I'm sure that at some point the story gets going, but I just wasn't interested in reading another 200-300 pages to find out.</span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer85272861">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8899807582757628983">I found this to be a very engaging Cold War story set in Russia &amp; shadowing the embassy lives of Sam Hollis, Lisa Rhodes, and Seth Alevy. An American tourist named Gregory Fisher alerts the embassy that he has come in contact with Major Jack Dodson, an escapee from Miss Ivanova's Charm School, the impressively successful espionage "school" where Russians are taught to become Americans and are used to gather intelligence in America. After Fisher turns up dead, Hollis is on a mission to find a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8899807582757628983">I found this to be a very engaging Cold War story set in Russia &amp; shadowing the embassy lives of Sam Hollis, Lisa Rhodes, and Seth Alevy. An American tourist named Gregory Fisher alerts the embassy that he has come in contact with Major Jack Dodson, an escapee from Miss Ivanova's Charm School, the impressively successful espionage "school" where Russians are taught to become Americans and are used to gather intelligence in America. After Fisher turns up dead, Hollis is on a mission to find and dismantle the school. <br /><br />It is fascinating how loyalty and betrayal coexist at even the highest levels. <br /><br />There were some parts in the middle that I could've done without, but I didn't want to stop reading near the end of the book. Definitely a heart-racing thriller. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8899807582757628983">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12302031600550153983">I read this years ago and found it so suspenseful that I couldn't put it down. The Charm School is a hidden "camp" in Russia where captured Americans are forced to teach KGB agents how to act American so as to blend in and spy in the U.S. Nelson DeMille is one of my favorite authors and he weaved a chilling action story taking place in the heart of the Cold War. I need to read this again!</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_166953239">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/166953239" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4463512-lindsey" class="left imgcol" title="Lindsey"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1292988256p2/4463512.jpg" alt="Lindsey" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/166953239?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 02, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4463512-lindsey" class="user" title="Lindsey">Lindsey</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/353814.The_Charm_School" title="Paperback 9780751531183" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer166953239">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12134799123353753859">This isn't the kind of book that I usually like, but I have to admit that I enjoyed it. I spent years studying Russia, and the Soviet version of Russia has always fascinated me. Granted, this book was highly imagined - but sometimes these types of far-fetched scenarios can be fun to explore as a sort of vacation from reality. <br /><br />There's a scene in the book where the two main characters are boarding a plane, waiting to fly out of Moscow to the safe haven of the West. I have to admit, I got incredibl</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12134799123353753859">This isn't the kind of book that I usually like, but I have to admit that I enjoyed it. I spent years studying Russia, and the Soviet version of Russia has always fascinated me. Granted, this book was highly imagined - but sometimes these types of far-fetched scenarios can be fun to explore as a sort of vacation from reality. <br /><br />There's a scene in the book where the two main characters are boarding a plane, waiting to fly out of Moscow to the safe haven of the West. I have to admit, I got incredibly tense (as tense as the characters were) remembering my own exit from Moscow in the post-Soviet year of 2006. Even though the country was supposedly democratic at the time and theoretically I had no reason to be tense, I was completely on edge while waiting for the plane to take off. Maybe it was the rigorous security search (they even rifled through individual pages of each book I had!), passport control, or the generally glum Soviet facade of the Sheremetevo airport that contributed to my paranoia... Regardless, as the book's characters anxiously awaited take-off and their ascent to safety, I was right there with them! And when something happened to keep them from leaving Russia (sorry for the spoiler), I was so upset that I had to put the book down for a couple days. <br /><br />As for me, I got out of Russia safely, but not without incident. Security, during their intensive search, discovered several embarrassing personal items (but no real contraband). And then my plane was hit by lightning immediately after take-off! Everyone screamed, the cabin powered down, and we all felt the plane drop. But planes are all well-grounded against lightning strikes, and about 3 seconds later the lights came back on and the plane continued its ascent. <br /><br />I personally took the lightning strike on the plane as Moscow's way of saying "And STAY out!" to me... <br /><br />All in all, the book was rather entertaining for a former Russophile. Definitely a guilty pleasure! </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12134799123353753859">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/142050891?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 28, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2176886-chris-schaeffer" class="user" title="Chris Schaeffer">Chris Schaeffer</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/353814.The_Charm_School" title="Paperback 9780751531183" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer142050891">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7332446045888103426">The Charm School by Nelson DeMille was an extremely long, detailed look into a fictional scenario in which the Russian KGB had a secret spy school for the past two decades. Despite the length of the book, over 700 pages in the paperback, I found the book to be engrossing from the beginning to the end. A flaw in many long books is the overwhelming number of characters, but DeMille doesn’t compound the complexity of this novel with too many characters. Instead he gives depth to a limited number of</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7332446045888103426">The Charm School by Nelson DeMille was an extremely long, detailed look into a fictional scenario in which the Russian KGB had a secret spy school for the past two decades. Despite the length of the book, over 700 pages in the paperback, I found the book to be engrossing from the beginning to the end. A flaw in many long books is the overwhelming number of characters, but DeMille doesn’t compound the complexity of this novel with too many characters. Instead he gives depth to a limited number of elite people in the story, including some crazed “bad guys” that Mr. DeMille brings to life so well in many of his books.<br /><br />Despite my little knowledge about Russia and its politics, this international spy novel leads the reader through the complex relationship that defined the Cold War between the United States and Russia. While the story immediately launches into an intriguing progression of events, the novel is much slower in the first half of the 700 pages, but the depth of characters and original plot kept me interested till the end.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7332446045888103426">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/12586877-paul-thompson" class="user" title="Paul Thompson">Paul Thompson</a>

          added it


          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer434689655">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9913176808017045676"> “Whenever you are unhappy, go to Russia. Anyone who has come to understand that country will find himself content to live anywhere else.” As the two countries patch their post-war relationship, a severe conflict in Nelson Demille’s The Charm School, threatens to destroy any trust built up between America and Russia. The life of a Russian common citizen is personally displayed and backed up by the constant stream of action filled plot.<br /> The story begins with Greg Fisher, a student from America cu</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9913176808017045676"> “Whenever you are unhappy, go to Russia. Anyone who has come to understand that country will find himself content to live anywhere else.” As the two countries patch their post-war relationship, a severe conflict in Nelson Demille’s The Charm School, threatens to destroy any trust built up between America and Russia. The life of a Russian common citizen is personally displayed and backed up by the constant stream of action filled plot.<br /> The story begins with Greg Fisher, a student from America currently on vacation. After a few bad decisions, Mr. Fisher finds himself in trouble with the KGB and resorting to the US Embassy stationed in Russia for help. The embassy gets word of suspicion of American soldiers being held captive to teach Russian soldiers the ways of the US. Mr. Fisher becomes mysteriously missing and soon dead, which increases the Embassy's strive to uncover the hidden actions of the Soviet Union.<br /> As the Embassy continues to solve the mystery of the “Charm School,” the reader witnesses the truth of the common Russian citizen. Lisa and Mr.Hollis, from the embassy, first immerse the reader when visiting Yablonya (a perfect example of the simple lifestyle of Russia). The folk of Yablonya were very hospitable and intensely interested in the America and the life outside Russia. After several rounds of Vodka shots, the citizens and the Embassy members begin to speak. Questions begin to swarm of what the Soviet Union has said about America is true and how America views them. The village wasn’t used to visitors so their reaction to Lisa and Mr.Hollis was very unsure, but also hospitable.<br /> The novel displays the tension between Russia and the US during the Cold War very neatly. The book gives a James Bond feel and is a great read for those interested in action and mystery. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9913176808017045676">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/395584-jim" class="user" title="Jim">Jim</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/353814.The_Charm_School" title="Paperback 9780751531183" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/395584-jim?shelf=thrillers" class="actionLinkLite">thrillers</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/395584-jim?shelf=ebooks" class="actionLinkLite">ebooks</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/395584-jim?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer806332426">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14781142338198863919">This one was a re-read for me of a title that just had to be added to my ebook collection when the price was right. When it first came out many years ago, it quickly vaulted to the top of my favorites list in the thrillers category, and the passage of time (and a couple of minor edits by DeMille) has done nothing to lessen my love for this one. It's simply a great thriller. Excellent premise, excellent characters, excellent narrative, excellent pacing. The only downside is that it lacks the stan</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14781142338198863919">This one was a re-read for me of a title that just had to be added to my ebook collection when the price was right. When it first came out many years ago, it quickly vaulted to the top of my favorites list in the thrillers category, and the passage of time (and a couple of minor edits by DeMille) has done nothing to lessen my love for this one. It's simply a great thriller. Excellent premise, excellent characters, excellent narrative, excellent pacing. The only downside is that it lacks the standout quality of dialogue of most of DeMille's other works. But then again, I consider DeMille to be unsurpassed at writing zippy and simply awesome dialogue, so even a relatively poor effort from him is going to be much better than most others' best efforts. The other thing that stands out in retrospect is that DeMille's poor regard for the CIA is nothing new, as the agency is shown here to be willing to go to great lengths to be messed-up when not being downright evil. In the end, though, if you want a classic espionage thriller, you can hardly go wrong with this one.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14781142338198863919">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_278868966">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/278868966" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2221534-brie" class="left imgcol" title="Brie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1253638832p2/2221534.jpg" alt="Brie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/278868966?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 16, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2221534-brie" class="user" title="Brie">Brie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1832655.The_Charm_School" title="Paperback 9780446675093" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2221534-brie?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2221534-brie?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer278868966">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15428082577624011871">I'm not sure how many years have gone by since I read this book but it has been quite a few. I initially picked it up after having read <a title="The General's Daughter by Nelson DeMille" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/98427.The_General_s_Daughter">The General's Daughter</a>, which I loved. But every other Nelson DeMille book I have read has fallen way short of my expectations.<br /><br />As I remember, this story was still pretty good and rather interesting, it just took awhile to get anywhere. DeMille tends to take his time getting his plots going (I remember The General's Daughter being an exception to this). This book</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15428082577624011871">I'm not sure how many years have gone by since I read this book but it has been quite a few. I initially picked it up after having read <a title="The General's Daughter by Nelson DeMille" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/98427.The_General_s_Daughter">The General's Daughter</a>, which I loved. But every other Nelson DeMille book I have read has fallen way short of my expectations.<br /><br />As I remember, this story was still pretty good and rather interesting, it just took awhile to get anywhere. DeMille tends to take his time getting his plots going (I remember The General's Daughter being an exception to this). This book takes place in Russia and revolves around a 'Charm School' set up in Russia with the intention of teaching Russians how to act like Americans so they can blend in here in America. And that's about all I remember. If you are thinking of reading DeMille, I would strongly suggest The General's Daughter over any of his other works.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15428082577624011871">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1350631967">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9771315886685832342">This tale of Cold War intrigue came very highly recommended. I am surprised to be so disappointed. Perhaps I shouldn’t have listened to The Charm School audio while reading Red Notice, the current real-life thriller, as I much preferred that story to this one. The Charm School felt formulaic, the characters weren’t interesting, and the story just went on and on. There wasn’t enough happening to warrant almost 25 hours of audio.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/8084975-laura" class="user" title="Laura">Laura</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer337631953">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4692065352644587433">After finishing the book, I've decided I liked it... It's another one of those "takes forever to get somewhere" kind of reads. Overall it's good but s l o w. There is a lot of superfluous text that made me skim through paragraphs (and pages) just to get to a pertinent part. It left me wishing it were condensed, moved faster and focused on the plot rather than adding so much needless information. I felt it was about 100 pages too long. The first 200 pages were painfully slow...but once the plot r</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4692065352644587433">After  finishing the book, I've decided I liked it... It's another one of those "takes forever to get somewhere" kind of reads. Overall it's good but s l o w. There is a lot of superfluous text that made me skim through paragraphs (and pages) just to get to a pertinent part. It left me wishing it were condensed, moved faster and focused on the plot rather than adding so much needless information. I felt it was about 100 pages too long. The first 200 pages were painfully slow...but once the plot really got rolling I was absorbed in the exciting conclusion. The main character's humor was enjoyable and the last 100+ were so exciting I stayed up waaaaay too late finishing the book. All in all...3 stars because 1/3 of the book was 1 star and the last 100 pages were 5 stars... So we'll split the difference!</span>
