<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_210491351">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/210491351" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4035000-laura-wood" class="left imgcol" title="Laura Wood"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1296534883p2/4035000.jpg" alt="Laura Wood" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/210491351?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 27, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4035000-laura-wood" class="user" title="Laura Wood">Laura Wood</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/353814.The_Charm_School" title="Paperback 9780751531183" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer210491351">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16495345562525196052">If I were to judge this book on plot alone, I would give it five stars. Set in the 1980s, The Charm School tells the story of U.S. government agents who attempt to rescue American POWs from Vietnam who were secretly shipped to the Soviet Union. The POWs then became "instructors" of American English and culture to Soviet agents who wanted to pass as Americans. I can imagine this book would have been terrifying in 1988 when it was published. Anyway, it was an interesting snapshot of the times and</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16495345562525196052">If I were to judge this book on plot alone, I would give it five stars. Set in the 1980s, The Charm School tells the story of U.S. government agents who attempt to rescue American POWs from Vietnam who were secretly shipped to the Soviet Union. The POWs then became "instructors" of American English and culture to Soviet agents who wanted to pass as Americans. I can imagine this book would have been terrifying in 1988 when it was published. Anyway, it was an interesting snapshot of the times and Russian culture (the parts that weren't completely stereotyped!). Unfortunately, the characters were not as well developed as the plot. The female lead, in particular, was so annoying that I wanted to hand her over to the KGB myself- call me a traitor if you will!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16495345562525196052">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16112354265170154822">The Charm School was the first Nelson DeMille book that I read many years ago. It was well written, exciting, and unforgettable. DeMille's books are responsible for many sleepless nights because it's impossible to put them down!</span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/470958758" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1127602-cyn" class="left imgcol" title="Cyn"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1309701976p2/1127602.jpg" alt="Cyn" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/470958758?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 03, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1127602-cyn" class="user" title="Cyn">Cyn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/353814.The_Charm_School" title="Paperback 9780751531183" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer470958758">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14338811491146664531">I normally wouldn't read a Cold War spy novel but so many readers I respect recommended this book, I decided to give it a go and I have to say it didn't disappoint. I grew up during the Cold War and I remember when the USSR was the Big Bad but this book really brought it all back, just how cold it was. There were a few moments that the whole thing seemed totally over the top but that didn't really infringe on my enjoyment of the story. The concept was compelling and I picked this book up at ever</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14338811491146664531">I normally wouldn't read a Cold War spy novel but so many readers I respect recommended this book, I decided to give it a go and I have to say it didn't disappoint. I grew up during the Cold War and I remember when the USSR was the Big Bad but this book really brought it all back, just how cold it was. There were a few moments that the whole thing seemed totally over the top but that didn't really infringe on my enjoyment of the story. The concept was compelling and I picked this book up at every chance I got to try to get in a few more pages. I will definitely read another of DeMille's books.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14338811491146664531">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TXpwyu8hOxafqgOIFIeE47hnri/7Eufac6YQFPgIfIwork8ZHfMv7BNydzNq5mJR8ZBtNrLPoHAZrxWGNJ2KyQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1238.Nelson_DeMille">About Nelson DeMille</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/1238.Nelson_DeMille"><img alt="1238" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1377030719p2/1238.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer11713353834083810638">Nelson Richard DeMille was born in New York City on August 23, 1943 to Huron and Antonia (Panzera) DeMille. He moved as a child with his family to Long Island. In high school, he played football and ran track.<br /><br />DeMille spent three years at Hofstra University, then joined the Army and attended Officer Candidate School. He was a First Lieutenant in the United States Army (1966-69) and saw action as an</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11713353834083810638">Nelson Richard DeMille was born in New York City on August 23, 1943 to Huron and Antonia (Panzera) DeMille. He moved as a child with his family to Long Island. In high school, he played football and ran track.<br /><br />DeMille spent three years at Hofstra University, then joined the Army and attended Officer Candidate School. He was a First Lieutenant in the United States Army (1966-69) and saw action as an infantry platoon leader with the First Cavalry Division in Vietnam. He was decorated with the Air Medal, Bronze Star, and the Vietnamese Cross of Gallantry.<br /><br />DeMille returned to the States and went back to Hofstra University where he received his degree in Political Science and History. He has three children, Lauren, Alexander, and James, and still lives on Long Island.<br /><br /> DeMille's earlier books were NYPD detective novels. His first major novel was By the Rivers of Babylon, published in 1978 and still in print, as are all his succeeding novels. He is a member of The Authors Guild, the Mystery Writers of America, and American Mensa. He was a past president of Mystery Writers of America and International Thriller Writers ThrillerMaster of the Year 2015. He holds three honorary doctorates: Doctor of Humane Letters from Hofstra University, Doctor of Literature from Long Island University, and Doctor of Humane Letters from Dowling College.<br /><br />Nelson DeMille is the author of: By the Rivers of Babylon, Cathedral, The Talbot Odyssey, Word of Honor, The Charm School, The Gold Coast, The General's Daughter, Spencerville, Plum Island, The Lion's Game, Up Country, Night Fall, Wild Fire, The Gate House, The Lion, The Panther, The Quest, and Radiant Angel. He also co-authored Mayday with Thomas Block and has contributed short stories, book reviews, and articles to magazines and newspapers. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11713353834083810638">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/1238.Nelson_DeMille" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Nelson DeMille...</a>
